there are more than 501 students in a school such that 20% of them exactly took physics and 28% of them exactly took math. What could be the least possible no of students in the school? Answer Choices: (A) 550 (B) 570 (C) 600 (D) 700 (E) none of these
Let's think step by step.
Let's assume that the least possible number of students in the school is $x$. 

We know that 20% of the students took physics, so the number of students who took physics is $0.2x$. Similarly, the number of students who took math is $0.28x$. 

Since we are looking for the least possible number of students, we want to minimize $x$. 

We know that the total number of students is greater than 501, so we can write the inequality $x > 501$. 

We also know that the number of students who took physics plus the number of students who took math is less than or equal to the total number of students. In other words, $0.2x + 0.28x \leq x$. 

Simplifying this inequality, we get $0.48x \leq x$. 

Dividing both sides of the inequality by $x$, we get $0.48 \leq 1$. 

Since $0.48$ is less than $1$, this inequality is always true. 

Therefore, the least possible number of students in the school is $\boxed{\textbf{(A) }550}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(A) }550}$.

2st data
The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k = Answer Choices: (A) 40 (B) 62 (C) 82 (D) 92 (E) 102
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the sum of the first k consecutive integers. We can use the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series, which is $\frac{n}{2}(a_1 + a_n)$, where n is the number of terms and $a_1$ and $a_n$ are the first and last terms, respectively.

In this case, the first term is -50 and the sum is 51, so we have $\frac{k}{2}(-50 + a_n) = 51$.

Next, let's find the last term, $a_n$. We know that the last term is $a_1 + (n-1)d$, where d is the common difference. In this case, the common difference is 1, so $a_n = -50 + (k-1)(1) = -50 + k - 1 = -49 + k$.

Substituting this into our equation, we have $\frac{k}{2}(-50 + (-49 + k)) = 51$.

Simplifying, we get $\frac{k}{2}(-99 + k) = 51$.

Multiplying both sides by 2, we have $k(-99 + k) = 102$.

Expanding, we get $-99k + k^2 = 102$.

Rearranging, we have $k^2 - 99k + 102 = 0$.

Factoring, we get $(k - 3)(k - 34) = 0$.

So, k = 3 or k = 34.

Since we are looking for the least integer, k = 3 is the answer.

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\text{(A) } 40}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\text{(A) } 40}$.

Let's think step by step.
First, let's calculate the interest earned every six months. The annual interest rate is 12%, so the interest earned every six months is 12%/2 = 6%.
Next, let's calculate the interest earned in the first six months. The bond has a face value of $5,000, so the interest earned in the first six months is 6% of $5,000 = $<<6*.01*5000=300>>300.

Since the interest is compounded every six months, the interest earned in the first year is $300 + $300 = $<<300+300=600>>600.

5st data
There is a 90% chance that a registered voter in Burghtown voted in the last election. If five registered voters are chosen at random, what is the approximate likelihood that exactly four of them voted in the last election? Answer Choices: (A) 26.2% (B) 32.8% (C) 43.7% (D) 59.0% (E) 65.6%
Let's think step by step.
We can use the binomial probability formula to solve this problem. The formula is given by $P(X=k) = \binom{n}{k} \cdot p^k \cdot (1-p)^{n-k}$, where $n$ is the number of trials, $k$ is the number of successful outcomes, and $p$ is the probability of success.

In this case, $n=5$ (since we are choosing 5 registered voters), $k=4$ (since we want exactly 4 of them to have voted), and $p=0.9$ (since there is a 90% chance that a registered voter voted in the last election).

Plugging these values into the formula, we get $P(X=4) = \binom{5}{4} \cdot 0.9^4 \cdot (1-0.9)^{5-4} = 5 \cdot 0.9^4 \cdot 0.1^1 = 0.32805$.

Therefore, the approximate likelihood that exactly four of the five registered voters voted in the last election is $\boxed{\textbf{(B) }32.8\%}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(B) }32.8\%}$.

1. Neha is 12th from the left end, so there are 11 children to the left of Neha.
2. Radha is 6th from the right end, so there are 5 children to the right of Radha.
3. When Radha is shifted to the left by 2 places, she will be at the 4th position from the right end.
4. When Neha is shifted to the right by 2 places, she will be at the 14th position from the left end.
5. There are 6 children between Radha and Neha, so there are 3 children to the right of Radha and 3 children to the left of Neha.
6. Therefore, there are 4 children to the right of Radha and 8 children to the left of Neha.
7. Since there are 11 children to the left of Neha and 8 children to the left of Neha, there are a total of 11 + 8 + 1 (Neha) = 20 children to the left of Radha.
8. Similarly, there are 5 children to the right of Radha and 3 children to the right of Radha, so there are a total of 5 + 3 + 1 (Radha) = 9 children to the right of Neha.
9. Therefore, the total number of children in the row is 20 + 9 = 29.
10. The answer is (E) 29.

The average cost per year of the new tires is what percent greater than the cost of repairing the current tires? Answer Choices: (A) 8% (B) 10% (C) 12.5% (D) 16.7% (E) 25%

Next, let's calculate the cost per year of repairing the current tires. Since the repair costs $40 per tire and makes the tires last for one additional year, the cost per year is $40/1 = $40 per year.

Now, let's calculate the percent difference between the cost per year of the new tires and the cost per year of repairing the current tires. The percent difference is given by (cost of new tires - cost of repairing current tires) / cost of repairing current tires * 100%.

Plugging in the values, we get (45 - 40) / 40 * 100% = 5 / 40 * 100% = 12.5%.

Therefore, the average cost per year of the new tires is 12.5% greater than the cost of repairing the current tires.

The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other? Answer Choices: (A) 3 hours (B) 5 hours (C) 6 hours (D) 4 hours (E) 7 hours
Let's think step by step.
First, we need to determine the relative speed between the two cars. Since they are traveling in the same direction, we subtract the slower car's speed from the faster car's speed: 55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph.

Next, we need to determine how long it will take for the cars to be 15 miles apart. We can use the formula distance = rate × time, where distance is 15 miles and rate is 3 mph. Plugging in these values, we get 15 miles = 3 mph × time.

To solve for time, we divide both sides of the equation by 3 mph: time = 15 miles / 3 mph = 5 hours.

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 5 hours.

A car finishes a journey in 20 hours at the speed of 60 km/hr. If the same distance is to be covered in 10 hours, how much speed does the car gain? Answer Choices: (A) 80 kmph (B) 50 kmph (C) 120 kmph (D) 70 kmph (E) 80 kmph
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the distance covered in 20 hours at a speed of 60 km/hr. We can use the formula distance = speed × time.

Distance = 60 km/hr × 20 hours = 1200 km

Now, let's find the new speed needed to cover the same distance in 10 hours. We can use the formula speed = distance ÷ time.

Speed = 1200 km ÷ 10 hours = 120 km/hr

To find the speed gained, we subtract the original speed from the new speed.

Speed gained = 120 km/hr - 60 km/hr = 60 km/hr

Therefore, the car gains a speed of 60 km/hr. The correct answer choice is (B) 50 kmph.

12st data
Amy is organizing her bookshelves and finds that she has 10 different types of books. She then codes each book with either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. If each type of book is uniquely represented by either a single letter or pair of letters, what is the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books? (Assume the order of letters in a pair does not matter.) Answer Choices: (A) 3 (B) 4 (C) 5 (D) 10 (E) 20
Let's think step by step.
First, let's consider the case where each type of book is represented by a single letter. In this case, we would need 10 different letters to represent the 10 types of books. Therefore, the minimum number of letters needed in this case is 10.

Now, let's consider the case where each type of book is represented by a pair of two different letters. In this case, we would need to choose 2 letters out of the 26 letters in the alphabet to form each pair. The number of ways to choose 2 letters out of 26 is given by the combination formula, which is $\binom{26}{2} = \frac{26!}{2!(26-2)!} = \frac{26 \cdot 25}{2} = 325$. Therefore, we would need 325 different pairs of letters to represent the 10 types of books.

Comparing the two cases, we can see that the minimum number of letters needed is 10, which is smaller than 325. Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D) }10}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(D) }10}$.

So, the age difference between R and Q is x years.

Let's assume that R's age is y years.

14st data
The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is: Answer Choices: (A) 2.6m (B) 3.9m (C) 4m (D) 4.2m (E) 4.4m
Let's think step by step.
Let's assume the height of the room is 2x and the semi-perimeter is 5x.

The perimeter of the room is 2 times the semi-perimeter, so it is 10x.

The length of the room is the perimeter divided by 2, so it is 5x.

The area of the walls is the length times the height, so it is 5x * 2x = 10x^2.

The cost of papering the walls is the area of the walls times the cost per square meter, so it is 10x^2 * 2 = 20x^2.

The area of the doors and windows is given as 15 sq.m.

The total area to be papered is the area of the walls minus the area of the doors and windows, so it is 20x^2 - 15.

The cost of papering the walls is given as Rs.260.

So, we have the equation 20x^2 - 15 = 260.

Adding 15 to both sides, we get 20x^2 = 275.

Dividing both sides by 20, we get x^2 = 13.75.

Taking the square root of both sides, we get x = √13.75.

Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 2√13.75.

Approximating the value of √13.75 to the nearest tenth, we get √13.75 ≈ 3.7.

Therefore, the height of the room is approximately 2 * 3.7 = 7.4.

Since the answer choices are given in meters, we need to convert 7.4 meters to the nearest tenth.

Therefore, the height of the room is approximately 7.4 meters, which is closest to 7.4.

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 3.9m.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 3.9m.

15st data
A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join? Answer Choices: (A) 2 months (B) 4 months (C) 23 months (D) 24 months (E) 84 months
Let's think step by step.
Let's start by finding the total investment in the business at the end of the year. 
A invested Rs.40,000 for the entire year, so his investment is Rs.40,000 * 12 = Rs.480,000.
B joined after 2 months, so his investment is Rs.60,000 * 10 = Rs.600,000.
C joined after B, so his investment is Rs.120,000 * x, where x is the number of months after B joined.
The total investment is Rs.480,000 + Rs.600,000 + Rs.120,000 * x = Rs.1,080,000 + Rs.120,000 * x.

Now, let's find the ratio of C's share to the total profit. 
C's share is Rs.150,000, so the ratio is Rs.150,000 / Rs.375,000 = 2/5.

Since C's share is 2/5 of the total profit, the ratio of C's investment to the total investment must also be 2/5. 
So, Rs.120,000 * x / (Rs.1,080,000 + Rs.120,000 * x) = 2/5.

Cross-multiplying, we get 5 * Rs.120,000 * x = 2 * (Rs.1,080,000 + Rs.120,000 * x).
Simplifying, we get 600,000x = 2,160,000 + 240,000x.
Combining like terms, we get 360,000x = 2,160,000.
Dividing both sides by 360,000, we get x = 6.

Therefore, C joined the business 6 months after B joined. 
Since B joined after 2 months, C joined after 2 + 6 = 8 months.
Therefore, the answer is (B) 8 months.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 8 months.

16st data
Janice bikes at 10 miles per hour, while Jennie bikes at 20. How long until they have collectively biked 1 mile? Answer Choices: (A) 1 minute (B) 2 minutes (C) 3 minutes (D) 4 minutes (E) 5 minutes
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find out how long it takes for Janice to bike 1 mile. Since she bikes at a speed of 10 miles per hour, it will take her $\frac{1}{10}$ of an hour to bike 1 mile. 

Next, let's find out how long it takes for Jennie to bike 1 mile. Since she bikes at a speed of 20 miles per hour, it will take her $\frac{1}{20}$ of an hour to bike 1 mile. 

Now, let's find out how long it takes for them to collectively bike 1 mile. We can add the times it takes for each of them to bike 1 mile. 

$\frac{1}{10} + \frac{1}{20} = \frac{2}{20} + \frac{1}{20} = \frac{3}{20}$

So, it takes them $\frac{3}{20}$ of an hour to collectively bike 1 mile. 

To convert this to minutes, we multiply by 60 since there are 60 minutes in an hour. 

$\frac{3}{20} \cdot 60 = \frac{3 \cdot 60}{20} = \frac{180}{20} = 9$

So, it takes them 9 minutes to collectively bike 1 mile. 

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\text{(E) }5 \text{ minutes}}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\text{(E) }5 \text{ minutes}}$.

18st data
All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm? Answer Choices: (A) 50 (B) 70 (C) 75 (D) 100 (E) 125
Let's think step by step.
Let's start by defining some variables:
Let V be the number of files infected by a virus.
Let W be the number of files infected by a worm.
Let B be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.

We are given that the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm. So, we can write the equation W - B = 2.5B.

We are also given that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus. This means that V = 0.5(250) = 125.

We know that the total number of files infected by either a virus or a worm is 250. So, we can write the equation V + W - B = 250.

Substituting V = 125 into the second equation, we get 125 + W - B = 250.

Substituting W - B = 2.5B into the second equation, we get 125 + 2.5B = 250.

Simplifying the equation, we get 2.5B = 125.

Dividing both sides of the equation by 2.5, we get B = 50.

Substituting B = 50 into the equation W - B = 2.5B, we get W - 50 = 2.5(50).

Simplifying the equation, we get W - 50 = 125.

Adding 50 to both sides of the equation, we get W = 175.

Now, we can find the number of files that were not infected by a worm by subtracting W from the total number of files: 250 - 175 = 75.

Therefore, the answer is (C) 75.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) 75.
pred_before : (C) 75.
pred_after : C

19st data
By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work? Answer Choices: (A) 4 (B) 8 (C) 22 (D) 50 (E) 20
Let's think step by step.
First, we need to find out how long it takes Jack to clean the entire yacht by himself. We are given that Jack can clean the yacht in 12 hours, so his rate of cleaning is 1 yacht per 12 hours.

Finally, we need to find out how long it takes Jill to finish the remaining work. Since Jill's rate of cleaning is 1/20 yachts per hour and there is 1/3 of the work left, it will take Jill 1/20 * 3 = 3/20 hours to finish the remaining work.

Finally, let's calculate the area of the triangle. The area of a triangle is given by the formula (base * height) / 2. Substituting the values we found, the area of the triangle is ((a - b) * (-y)) / 2.

A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another? Answer Choices: (A) 1 hr 23 min (B) 1 hr 15 min (C) 1 hr 8 min (D) 56 min (E) 55 min
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Determine the time it takes for train M to travel from City A to the point of intersection.
Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am, so it takes 4 hours for train M to travel from City A to City B.

Step 2: Determine the time it takes for train N to travel from City B to the point of intersection.
Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am, so it takes 3.5 hours for train N to travel from City B to City A.

Step 3: Determine the time difference between the departure of train M and train N.
Train N departs 2 hours after train M (7 am - 5 am = 2 hours).

Step 4: Determine the time it takes for the two trains to meet.
Since train M takes 4 hours to travel from City A to City B and train N takes 3.5 hours to travel from City B to City A, the total time for the two trains to meet is 4 hours + 3.5 hours = 7.5 hours.

Step 5: Determine the time at which the two trains meet.
Train M departs at 5 am and the two trains meet after 7.5 hours, so the two trains meet at 5 am + 7.5 hours = 12:30 pm.

Step 6: Determine the time difference between the departure of train N and the time at which the two trains meet.
Train N departs at 7 am and the two trains meet at 12:30 pm, so the time difference is 12:30 pm - 7 am = 5.5 hours.

Step 7: Convert the time difference to minutes.
5.5 hours * 60 minutes/hour = 330 minutes.

Step 8: Determine the time in minutes.
330 minutes = 5 hours + 30 minutes = 5 hours 30 minutes.

Step 9: Determine the time in hours and minutes.
5 hours 30 minutes = 5 hours + 30 minutes = 5:30.

Therefore, the two trains cross each other at 5:30 pm.

But, if Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal. How much money does each have? Answer Choices: (A) 62, 35 (B) 62, 34 (C) 34, 62 (D) 42, 62 (E) 62, 42
Let's think step by step.
Let's assume that Arjun has x dollars and Sajal has y dollars.
According to the given information, if Arjun gives $30 to Sajal, Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun.
So, after Arjun gives $30 to Sajal, Sajal will have y + 30 dollars and Arjun will have x - 30 dollars.
Therefore, we can write the first equation as:
y + 30 = 2(x - 30)
Simplifying this equation, we get:
y + 30 = 2x - 60
y = 2x - 90 ...........(1)
Now, let's consider the second scenario where Sajal gives $10 to Arjun.
After Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have x + 10 dollars and Sajal will have y - 10 dollars.
According to the given information, Arjun will have thrice as much money as is left with Sajal.
So, we can write the second equation as:
x + 10 = 3(y - 10)
Simplifying this equation, we get:
x + 10 = 3y - 30
x = 3y - 40 ...........(2)
Now, we have two equations (1) and (2) with two variables (x and y).
We can solve these equations simultaneously to find the values of x and y.
Substituting the value of y from equation (1) into equation (2), we get:
x = 3(2x - 90) - 40
x = 6x - 270 - 40
x - 6x = -310
-5x = -310
x = -310/-5
x = 62
Substituting the value of x = 62 into equation (1), we get:
y = 2(62) - 90
y = 124 - 90
y = 34
Therefore, Arjun has $62 and Sajal has $34.
So, the answer is (C) 34, 62.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) 34, 62.

Let's think step by step.
Let's say that the original amount of dog food in the bowl was $x$.

At 9:00 am, the dog has eaten $\frac{1}{3}$ of the remaining food, so there is $\frac{2}{3} \cdot x$ left.

At 10:00 am, the dog has eaten $\frac{1}{3}$ of the remaining food, so there is $\frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot x$ left.

At 11:00 am, the dog has eaten $\frac{1}{3}$ of the remaining food, so there is $\frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot x$ left.

At 12:00 pm, the dog has eaten $\frac{1}{3}$ of the remaining food, so there is $\frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot x$ left.

Simplifying, we find that there is $\left(\frac{2}{3}\right)^4 \cdot x = \frac{16}{81} \cdot x$ left.

To find the percent of the original food remaining, we divide the amount remaining by the original amount and multiply by 100:

$\frac{\frac{16}{81} \cdot x}{x} \cdot 100 = \frac{16}{81} \cdot 100 = \frac{1600}{81} \approx \boxed{\textbf{(E) } 40\%}$.

31st data
There are 10 oranges in a basket. Find the no. of ways in which 2 oranges are chosen from the basket? Answer Choices: (A) 45 (B) 90 (C) 120 (D) 150 (E) 180
Let's think step by step.
To find the number of ways to choose 2 oranges from a basket of 10, we can use the combination formula. The formula for combinations is $\binom{n}{r}=\frac{n!}{r!(n-r)!}$, where $n$ is the total number of objects and $r$ is the number of objects being chosen.

In this case, we have 10 oranges and we want to choose 2. Plugging these values into the combination formula, we get $\binom{10}{2}=\frac{10!}{2!(10-2)!}=\frac{10!}{2!8!}=\frac{10\times9}{2\times1}=45$.

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\text{(A) } 45}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\text{(A) } 45}$.

40st data
On a test the passing students had an average of 83, while the failing students had an average
of 55. If the overall class average was 76, what percent of the class passed? Answer Choices: (A) 44% (B) 66% (C) 68% (D) 72% (E) 75%
Let's think step by step.
Let's assume that there are a total of 100 students in the class.

If the overall class average was 76, then the sum of all the test scores in the class is 76 * 100 = 7600.

Let's assume that there are x passing students in the class. Then, there are (100 - x) failing students.

The sum of the passing students' test scores is 83x, and the sum of the failing students' test scores is 55(100 - x).

Since the sum of all the test scores is 7600, we can write the equation: 83x + 55(100 - x) = 7600.

Simplifying the equation, we get: 83x + 5500 - 55x = 7600.

Combining like terms, we get: 28x + 5500 = 7600.

Subtracting 5500 from both sides, we get: 28x = 2100.

Dividing both sides by 28, we get: x = 75.

Therefore, there are 75 passing students in the class.

To find the percentage of the class that passed, we divide the number of passing students by the total number of students and multiply by 100.

The percentage of the class that passed is (75/100) * 100 = 75%.

Therefore, the answer is (E) 75%.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(E) 75%.
pred_before : (E) 75%.
pred_after : E
pred : E
GT : E

41st data
A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere? Answer Choices: (A)  13.3542 (B)  15.8113 (C)  18.3451 (D)  19.5667 (E)  20.8888
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the length of the space diagonal of the rectangular solid. The space diagonal is the line segment connecting two opposite vertices of the rectangular solid. Using the Pythagorean Theorem, we can find the length of the space diagonal.

The length of the space diagonal is $\sqrt{3^2+4^2+15^2}=\sqrt{9+16+225}=\sqrt{250}=5\sqrt{10}$.

Since the space diagonal of the rectangular solid is also the diameter of the sphere, the diameter of the sphere is $5\sqrt{10}$.

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\text{(A) } 13.3542}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\text{(A) } 13.3542}$.
pred_before : $\boxed{\text{(A) } 13.3542}$.

Points A, B, C, D lie in this order on the circumference of a circle. Minor arc AC is 160°, and minor arc BD is 150°. If B bisects minor arc AC, then what is the measure of minor arc AD? Answer Choices: (A) 80° (B) 130° (C) 140° (D) 160° (E) 220°
Let's think step by step.
First, let's draw a diagram to visualize the problem. 

[asy]
pair A, B, C, D, O;
O = (0,0);
A = dir(0);
B = dir(160);
C = dir(320);
D = dir(470);
draw(Circle(O,1));
draw(A--B--C--D--A);
label("$A$",A,dir(A));
label("$B$",B,dir(B));
label("$C$",C,dir(C));
label("$D$",D,dir(D));
[/asy]

We are given that minor arc AC is 160° and minor arc BD is 150°. Since B bisects minor arc AC, we can conclude that minor arc AB has a measure of 80°. 

[asy]
pair A, B, C, D, O;
O = (0,0);
A = dir(0);
B = dir(160);
C = dir(320);
D = dir(470);
draw(Circle(O,1));
draw(A--B--C--D--A);
label("$A$",A,dir(A));
label("$B$",B,dir(B));
label("$C$",C,dir(C));
label("$D$",D,dir(D));
label("$80^\circ$",A--B,dir(90));
[/asy]

Since the sum of the measures of minor arcs AB and BD is equal to the measure of minor arc AD, we can conclude that minor arc AD has a measure of $80^\circ + 150^\circ = \boxed{230^\circ}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\text{(E) } 220^\circ}$.

A book was sold for Rs 27.50 with a profit of 10%. If it were sold for Rs. 25.75, then would have been percentage of profit and loss ? Answer Choices: (A) 2% Profit (B) 3% Profit (C) 2% Loss (D) 3% Loss (E) 4% Loss
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Find the cost price of the book.
To find the cost price, we need to divide the selling price by 1 plus the profit percentage.
Cost price = Selling price / (1 + Profit percentage)
Cost price = 27.50 / (1 + 0.10)
Cost price = 27.50 / 1.10
Cost price = 25

Step 2: Find the profit or loss percentage.
Profit or loss percentage = (Selling price - Cost price) / Cost price * 100
Profit or loss percentage = (25.75 - 25) / 25 * 100
Profit or loss percentage = 0.75 / 25 * 100
Profit or loss percentage = 3%

Therefore, the answer is (D) 3% Loss.

50 additional quarter miles + 1 first quarter mile = 51 quarter miles

Finally, we need to convert the quarter miles to miles. Since there are 4 quarter miles in 1 mile, we can divide the total number of quarter miles by 4 to find the total number of miles we can travel: 

51 quarter miles / 4 = 12.75 miles

Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50 is 12.75 miles.

Last year, a Home Appliance Store sold an average(arithmetic mean) of 42 microwave ovens per month. In the first 10 months of this year,the store has sold an average(arithmetic mean) of only 20 microwave ovens per month. What was the average number of microwave ovens sold per month during the entire 22 months period ? Answer Choices: (A) 21 (B) 30 (C) 31 (D) 32 (E) None of the above
Let's think step by step.
To find the average number of microwave ovens sold per month during the entire 22-month period, we need to find the total number of microwave ovens sold and divide it by 22.

In the first 10 months of this year, the store sold an average of 20 microwave ovens per month. So, the total number of microwave ovens sold in the first 10 months is 20 * 10 = 200.

In the remaining 12 months of last year, the store sold an average of 42 microwave ovens per month. So, the total number of microwave ovens sold in the remaining 12 months is 42 * 12 = 504.

Therefore, the total number of microwave ovens sold during the entire 22-month period is 200 + 504 = 704.

To find the average, we divide the total number of microwave ovens sold by 22: 704 / 22 = 32.

Therefore, the average number of microwave ovens sold per month during the entire 22-month period is 32.

The answer is (D) 32.

Let's think step by step.
If exactly 2/5th of the children in the class are girls, then 3/5th of the children are boys. Since there are 100 boys in the class, we can set up the equation $\frac{3}{5} \cdot \text{total number of children} = 100$. Solving for the total number of children, we find that there are $\frac{5}{3} \cdot 100 = 166.\overline{6}$ children in the class. Since we can't have a fraction of a child, we round down to the nearest whole number, which is 166. 

To find the number of girls in the class, we multiply the total number of children by the fraction of girls, which is $\frac{2}{5}$. So, the number of girls is $\frac{2}{5} \cdot 166 = 66.\overline{6}$. Rounding down to the nearest whole number, we find that there are $\boxed{\textbf{(A) } 50}$ girls in the class.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(A) } 50}$.

53st data
The telephone bill of a certain establishment is party fixed and partly varies as the number of calls consumed. When in a certain month 540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800. In another month 620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040. In another month 500 units are consumed due to more
holidays. The bill for that month would be : Answer Choices: (A) Rs.1560 (B) Rs.1680 (C) Rs.1840 (D) Rs.1950 (E) Rs.1690
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Determine the fixed cost
To determine the fixed cost, we need to find the portion of the bill that does not change regardless of the number of calls consumed. We can do this by subtracting the variable cost from the total bill when the number of calls is known.

When 540 calls are consumed, the bill is Rs.1800.
Let's assume the variable cost per call is x.
So, the fixed cost can be calculated as follows:
Fixed cost = Total bill - Variable cost
Fixed cost = Rs.1800 - (540 * x)

Step 2: Determine the variable cost per call
To determine the variable cost per call, we can use the information given in the second scenario.
When 620 calls are consumed, the bill is Rs.2040.
Using the fixed cost calculated in step 1, we can calculate the variable cost per call as follows:
Variable cost per call = (Total bill - Fixed cost) / Number of calls
Variable cost per call = (Rs.2040 - Fixed cost) / 620

Step 3: Calculate the bill for 500 calls
Now that we have the fixed cost and the variable cost per call, we can calculate the bill for 500 calls.
Bill for 500 calls = Fixed cost + (Variable cost per call * 500)
Bill for 500 calls = (Rs.1800 - (540 * x)) + ((Rs.2040 - Fixed cost) / 620) * 500

Simplifying the equation:
Bill for 500 calls = Rs.1800 - (540 * x) + (Rs.2040 - Fixed cost) * (500 / 620)

Step 4: Substitute the value of Fixed cost
From step 1, we found that the fixed cost is Rs.1800 - (540 * x).
Substituting this value into the equation from step 3, we get:
Bill for 500 calls = Rs.1800 - (540 * x) + (Rs.2040 - (Rs.1800 - (540 * x))) * (500 / 620)

Simplifying the equation further:
Bill for 500 calls = Rs.1800 - (540 * x) + (Rs.2040 - Rs.1800 + (540 * x)) * (500 / 620)
Bill for 500 calls = Rs.1800 - (540 * x) + (240 + (540 * x)) * (500 /
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) Rs.1840

Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need? Answer Choices: (A) 58 (B) 62 (C) 66 (D) 70 (E) 74
Let's think step by step.
Let the length of the rectangular yard be $l$ and the width be $w$. We are given that the area of the yard is $240$ square meters, so we have the equation $lw=240$. 

We are also given that Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of the yard and leave one side of $10$ meters unfenced. Since the unfenced side is $10$ meters, we know that the width of the yard is $w=10$. 

Substituting this into our equation $lw=240$, we have $l(10)=240$, which simplifies to $l=24$. 

Now we know that the length of the yard is $l=24$ and the width is $w=10$. 

To find the amount of fencing Alice needs, we need to find the perimeter of the yard. The perimeter is the sum of the lengths of all four sides. 

The length of the three fenced sides is $2l+2w=2(24)+2(10)=48+20=68$. 

Therefore, Alice needs $68$ meters of fencing. 

The answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }66}$.

Let's think step by step.
First, we know that x < 0, which means x is negative. 
Next, we know that y > 0, which means y is positive. 
Now, let's consider the inequality |x^3| > |y^2|. 
Since x is negative, x^3 will also be negative. Therefore, |x^3| will be equal to -x^3. 
Since y is positive, y^2 will also be positive. Therefore, |y^2| will be equal to y^2. 
So, the inequality becomes -x^3 > y^2. 
Now, let's analyze the answer choices: 
(A) x > y: We cannot determine the relationship between x and y based on the given information, so this is not necessarily true. 
(B) y^2 > x^2: We cannot determine the relationship between y^2 and x^2 based on the given information, so this is not necessarily true. 
(C) -x^3 < y^2: This is true based on the given inequality -x^3 > y^2. 
(D) –x < y: We cannot determine the relationship between -x and y based on the given information, so this is not necessarily true. 
(E) x < –y: We cannot determine the relationship between x and -y based on the given information, so this is not necessarily true. 
Therefore, the only statement that must be true is (C) -x^3 < y^2.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) -x^3 < y^2.

Let's think step by step.
Let's start by setting up an equation to represent the given information. Let's call the cost of the appliance "x". 

The retailer sold the appliance for 40 percent above cost, which means the selling price is 100 percent (the cost) plus 40 percent (the profit). 

So, the selling price is 100 percent + 40 percent = 140 percent of the cost. 

We can write this as: 1.4x = selling price. 

We also know that the gross profit is $20.00. 

So, the selling price minus the cost equals the profit: selling price - x = $20.00. 

Now we can substitute the value of the selling price from the first equation into the second equation: 

1.4x - x = $20.00. 

Simplifying the equation, we get: 0.4x = $20.00. 

Dividing both sides of the equation by 0.4, we get: x = $50.00. 

Therefore, the cost of the appliance is $50.00. 

To find the selling price, we can substitute this value back into the first equation: 

1.4($50.00) = $70.00. 

Therefore, the retailer sold the appliance for $70.00. 

The correct answer choice is (D) $70.00.

Let's think step by step.

According to the given information, the total amount of money they planned to spend on eatables is Rs. 96.

So, each person's share would be 96/x.

However, 4 friends did not turn up, so the remaining friends had to contribute Rs. 4 extra each.

This means that each person's share increased to (96/x) + 4.

Since the remaining friends had to contribute Rs. 4 extra each, the total amount of money they contributed extra is 4 * (x - 4).

So, the total amount of money they actually spent on eatables is 96 + 4 * (x - 4).

Since the total amount of money they actually spent on eatables is equal to the sum of each person's share, we can set up the equation:

96 + 4 * (x - 4) = x * ((96/x) + 4)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

96 + 4x - 16 = 96 + 4x

Cancelling out the common terms, we get:

-16 = 0

This is not possible, so there is no solution to this equation.

Therefore, there is no possible number of friends who attended the picnic.

58st data
Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg. Answer Choices: (A) 50 % (B) 60 % (C) 55 % (D) 70 % (E) 58%
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Calculate the total cost of purchasing 90 kg of oranges.
The cost per kg is Rs. 450 / 90 kg = Rs. 5 per kg.

Step 2: Calculate the total revenue from selling 90 kg of oranges.
The revenue per kg is Rs. 7.50 per kg.

Total revenue = Rs. 7.50 per kg * 90 kg = Rs. 675.

Step 3: Calculate the profit.
Profit = Total revenue - Total cost = Rs. 675 - Rs. 450 = Rs. 225.

Step 4: Calculate the percentage gain.
Percentage gain = (Profit / Total cost) * 100% = (225 / 450) * 100% = 50%.

Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%. The correct answer choice is (A) 50%.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(A) 50%.

59st data
A bag contains 11 candy bars: three cost 50 cents each, four cost $1 each and four cost $2
each. How many ways can 3 candy bars be selected from the 11 candy bars so that the total cost is more than $4? Answer Choices: (A) 8 (B) 28 (C) 46 (D) 66 (E) 70
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Count the number of ways to select 3 candy bars without considering the cost.
We can use combinations to count the number of ways to select 3 candy bars from the 11 available. This can be calculated as C(11, 3) = 165.

Step 2: Count the number of ways to select 3 candy bars with a total cost of $4 or less.
We need to consider the different combinations of candy bars that can be selected with a total cost of $4 or less. Let's break it down into cases:

Case 1: Selecting all three candy bars that cost 50 cents each.
There are C(3, 3) = 1 way to select all three candy bars that cost 50 cents each.

Case 2: Selecting two candy bars that cost $1 each and one candy bar that costs 50 cents.
There are C(4, 2) = 6 ways to select two candy bars that cost $1 each from the four available. For each of these combinations, there are C(3, 1) = 3 ways to select one candy bar that costs 50 cents from the three available. So, there are a total of 6 * 3 = 18 ways to select two $1 candy bars and one 50 cent candy bar.

Case 3: Selecting one candy bar that costs $2 and two candy bars that cost 50 cents each.
There are C(4, 1) = 4 ways to select one candy bar that costs $2 from the four available. For each of these combinations, there are C(3, 2) = 3 ways to select two candy bars that cost 50 cents each from the three available. So, there are a total of 4 * 3 = 12 ways to select one $2 candy bar and two 50 cent candy bars.

Adding up the number of ways from each case, we have a total of 1 + 18 + 12 = 31 ways to select 3 candy bars with a total cost of $4 or less.

Step 3: Subtract the number of ways to select 3 candy bars with a total cost of $4 or less from the total number of ways to select 3 candy bars.
From step 1, we know that there are 165 ways to select 3 candy bars without considering the cost. From step 2, we know that there are 31 ways to select 
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is165 - 31 = 134 ways to select 3 candy bars with a total cost of more than $4.

However, we need to be careful because some of these combinations may have duplicate candy bars. For example, selecting three candy bars that cost $2 each would be counted multiple times. To account for this, we need to subtract the number of combinations that have duplicate candy bars.

Case 4: Selecting three candy bars that cost $2 each.
There are C(4, 3) = 4 ways to select three candy bars that cost $2 each from the four available.

Case 5: Selecting two candy bars that cost $2 each and one candy bar that costs $1.
There are C(4, 2) = 6 ways to select two candy bars that cost $2 each from the four available. For each of these combinations, there are C(4, 1) = 4 ways to select one candy bar that costs $1 from the four available. So, there are a total of 6 * 4 = 24 ways to select two $2 candy bars and one $1 candy bar.

Adding up the number of ways from each case, we have a total of 4 + 24 = 28 ways to select 3 candy bars with duplicate candy bars.

Subtracting the number of ways with duplicate candy bars from the total number of ways, we have 134 - 28 = 106 ways to select 3 candy bars with a total cost of more than $4.

Therefore, the answer is (B) 28.
pred_before : 165 - 31 = 134 ways to select 3 candy bars with a total cost of more than $4.

However, we need to be careful because some of these combinations may have duplicate candy bars. For example, selecting three candy bars that cost $2 each would be counted multiple times. To account for this, we need to subtract the number of combinations that have duplicate candy bars.

Case 4: Selecting three candy bars that cost $2 each.
There are C(4, 3) = 4 ways to select three candy bars that cost $2 each from the four available.

Case 5: Selecting two candy bars that cost $2 each and one candy bar that costs $1.
There are C(4, 2) = 6 ways to select two candy bars that cost $2 each from the four available. For each of these combinations, there are C(4, 1) = 4 ways to select one candy bar that costs $1 from the four available. So, there are a total of 6 * 4 = 24 ways to select two $2 candy bars and one $1 candy bar.

Adding up the number of ways from each case, we have a total of 4 + 24 = 28 ways to select 3 candy bars with duplicate candy bars.

Subtracting the number of ways with duplicate candy bars from the total number of ways, we have 134 - 28 = 106 ways to select 3 candy bars with a total cost of more than $4.

Therefore, the answer is (B) 28.

Let's think step by step.
We are given that the probability of event A occurring is 0.6. Since events A and B are independent, the probability of event B occurring is also 0.6.

We are also given that the probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is 0.96. This means that the probability of neither event A nor event B occurring is 1 - 0.96 = 0.04.

Since events A and B are independent, the probability of neither event A nor event B occurring is the product of the probabilities of each event not occurring. Therefore, we have:

(1 - 0.6)(1 - 0.6) = 0.04

Simplifying this equation, we get:

0.4 * 0.4 = 0.04

0.16 = 0.04

Therefore, the probability of event B occurring is 0.4.

The answer is (A) 0.5.

Let's think step by step.
Let the side length of the original square piece of cloth be $x$. After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the rectangular piece has dimensions $x-4$ by $x$. 

[asy]
pair A,B,C,D;
A=(0,0);
B=(0,1);
C=(1,1);
D=(1,0);
draw(A--B--C--D--cycle);
label("$x$",(0.5,0),S);
label("$x-4$",(0,0.5),W);
[/asy]

When this rectangular piece is cut in half diagonally, we get two congruent triangles. The area of each triangle is $\frac{1}{2} \cdot (x-4) \cdot x = 70$. Simplifying, we have $(x-4)x = 140$. Expanding, we have $x^2 - 4x = 140$. Rearranging, we have $x^2 - 4x - 140 = 0$. Factoring, we have $(x-14)(x+10) = 0$. Since the side length of a square cannot be negative, we have $x = 14$.

pair A,B,C,D;

C=(1,1);
D=(1,0);
draw(A--B--C--D--cycle);
label("$14$",(0.5,0),S);
label("$10$",(0,0.5),W);
[/asy]

Therefore, the original square piece of cloth had side length 14 feet. The perimeter of the square is $4 \cdot 14 = \boxed{\textbf{(D) } 62}$ feet.

Step 2: Calculate the total amount to be paid.

66st data
A coin made of alloy of aluminum and silver measures 2 x 15 mm (it is 2 mm thick and its diameter is 15 mm). If the weight of the coin is 30 grams and the volume of aluminum in the alloy equals that of silver, what will be the weight of a coin measuring 1 x 30 mm made of pure aluminum if silver is twice as heavy as aluminum? Answer Choices: (A) 36 grams (B) 40 grams (C) 42 grams (D) 48 grams (E) 50 grams
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the volume of the coin made of aluminum and silver. The volume of a cylinder is given by the formula V = πr^2h, where r is the radius and h is the height. Since the diameter is 15 mm, the radius is 15/2 = 7.5 mm = 0.75 cm. The height is 2 mm = 0.2 cm. Therefore, the volume of the coin is V = π(0.75)^2(0.2) = 0.3536 cm^3.

Since the volume of aluminum in the alloy equals that of silver, the volume of aluminum in the coin is 0.3536/2 = 0.1768 cm^3.

Next, let's find the weight of the aluminum in the coin. Since silver is twice as heavy as aluminum, the weight of the silver in the coin is 30/3 = 10 grams. Therefore, the weight of the aluminum in the coin is also 10 grams.

Now, let's find the weight of the pure aluminum coin measuring 1 x 30 mm. The volume of a cylinder is given by the formula V = πr^2h, where r is the radius and h is the height. Since the diameter is 30 mm, the radius is 30/2 = 15 mm = 1.5 cm. The height is 1 mm = 0.1 cm. Therefore, the volume of the pure aluminum coin is V = π(1.5)^2(0.1) = 0.7069 cm^3.

Since the weight of the aluminum in the alloy coin is 10 grams, and the volume of the aluminum in the alloy coin is 0.1768 cm^3, the weight of the pure aluminum coin is (10/0.1768) * 0.7069 = 40 grams.

Therefore, the weight of a coin measuring 1 x 30 mm made of pure aluminum is 40 grams. The answer is (B) 40 grams.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 40 grams.

Step 4: We want to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers. Let's call this average score a. This can be written as (sum of other scores)/(z-2) = a.

$x + y = 1000$

$x = 628$

77st data
John likes to have lightly flavored tea every evening. In a 50% strong milk tea, he replaces 15% of it with milk twice. Then, he replaces 10 percent of the resultant solution with more milk.
What is the final concentration of tea John drinks? Answer Choices: (A) 15.38% (B) 42% (C) 39.86% (D) 22.35% (E) 32.51%
Let's think step by step.
Let's start by assuming that John starts with 100 mL of 50% strong milk tea. 

First, he replaces 15% of it with milk twice. This means he removes 15 mL of the tea and replaces it with 15 mL of milk, and then repeats the process. After the first replacement, he has 85 mL of the 50% strong milk tea. After the second replacement, he has 85 mL * 0.85 = 72.25 mL of the 50% strong milk tea.

Next, he replaces 10% of the resultant solution with more milk. This means he removes 10% of the 72.25 mL of the 50% strong milk tea and replaces it with 10% of milk. After this replacement, he has 72.25 mL * 0.9 = 64.525 mL of the 50% strong milk tea.

To find the final concentration of tea, we need to divide the amount of tea (in mL) by the total volume of the solution (in mL) and multiply by 100%. The amount of tea in the solution is 64.525 mL * 0.5 (since the 50% strong milk tea is 50% tea) = 32.2625 mL.

The total volume of the solution is 64.525 mL + 10% of 64.525 mL (since he added 10% milk) = 64.525 mL + 6.4525 mL = 70.9775 mL.

The final concentration of tea is 32.2625 mL / 70.9775 mL * 100% = 45.45%.

Let's think step by step.
First, let's choose one point to be the center of the quadrilateral. Since F is already the center of the pentagon, we have 1 choice for the center point.

Next, let's choose the other three points to form the quadrilateral. We have 4 remaining points to choose from (A, B, C, and D), so we have 4 choices for the first point, 3 choices for the second point, and 2 choices for the third point.

Therefore, the total number of different quadrilaterals that can be formed is 1 * 4 * 3 * 2 = 24.

However, we have overcounted some quadrilaterals. For example, if we choose points A, B, C, and D in that order, we get the same quadrilateral as if we choose points B, A, D, and C in that order. Therefore, we need to divide by 4! (the number of ways to arrange the 4 points) to correct for this overcounting.

So, the final answer is 24 / 4! = 24 / 24 = 1.

Therefore, there is only 1 different quadrilateral that can be formed by joining 4 of the points A, B, C, D, E, and F.

At a conference, one team is made up of 4 men and 4 women. Four presenters are chosen to present the team's findings in front of the entire conference. How many different groups of presenters can be chosen from the team if a team cannot be composed of men only or women only? (Two groups of presenters are considered different if at least one presenter is different.) Answer Choices: (A) 120 (B) 19 (C) 180 (D) 420 (E) 460
Let's think step by step.
First, let's consider the case where the group of presenters must include at least one man and one woman. In this case, we have 4 choices for the first presenter (any of the 4 men), and 4 choices for the second presenter (any of the 4 women). After choosing the first two presenters, we have 3 choices for the third presenter (either a man or a woman who hasn't been chosen yet), and 2 choices for the fourth presenter (the remaining person of the opposite gender). Therefore, there are $4 \cdot 4 \cdot 3 \cdot 2 = 96$ possible groups of presenters in this case.

Next, let's consider the case where the group of presenters is composed entirely of men. In this case, we have 4 choices for each presenter, so there are $4 \cdot 4 \cdot 4 \cdot 4 = 256$ possible groups of presenters.

Similarly, if the group of presenters is composed entirely of women, there are also 256 possible groups of presenters.

Therefore, the total number of possible groups of presenters is $96 + 256 + 256 = 608$.

However, we need to subtract the cases where the group of presenters is composed entirely of men or entirely of women, since these cases are not allowed.

So, the final answer is $608 - 256 - 256 = \boxed{\textbf{(E) }460}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(E) }460}$.

99st data
At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit? Answer Choices: (A) 1,879 (B) 1,875 (C) 1,876 (D) 1,872 (E) 1,800
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Calculate the cost price of the sewing machine.
The cost price of the sewing machine is given as Rs. 1200/-.

Step 2: Calculate the selling price after offering a 20% discount.
To calculate the selling price after offering a 20% discount, we need to subtract 20% of the cost price from the cost price.
20% of Rs. 1200/- = (20/100) * 1200 = Rs. 240/-
Selling price = Cost price - Discount = Rs. 1200 - Rs. 240 = Rs. 960/-

Step 3: Calculate the selling price that gives a 20% profit.
To calculate the selling price that gives a 20% profit, we need to add 20% of the cost price to the cost price.
20% of Rs. 1200/- = (20/100) * 1200 = Rs. 240/-
Selling price = Cost price + Profit = Rs. 1200 + Rs. 240 = Rs. 1440/-

Step 4: Calculate the selling price after offering a 20% discount and making a 20% profit.
To calculate the selling price after offering a 20% discount and making a 20% profit, we need to add 20% of the selling price to the selling price.
20% of Rs. 1440/- = (20/100) * 1440 = Rs. 288/-
Selling price = Selling price + Profit = Rs. 1440 + Rs. 288 = Rs. 1728/-

Step 5: Calculate the price at which the sewing machine should be marked.

Let's think step by step.
To find P(A/B), we can use the formula for conditional probability:

P(A/B) = P(A and B) / P(B)

Since A and B are independent events, P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).

P(A/B) = P(A) * P(B) / P(B)

P(A/B) = P(A)

Let's think step by step.
We know that the quadratic equation has the form $x^2 + mx + 22 = 0$. We are given that one of the roots is $1.5$. 

Since the quadratic equation has real coefficients, the other root must also be real. Therefore, the quadratic equation can be factored as $(x - 1.5)(x - r) = 0$, where $r$ is the other root.

Expanding this equation, we get $x^2 - (1.5 + r)x + 1.5r = 0$.

Comparing this with the given quadratic equation $x^2 + mx + 22 = 0$, we can equate the coefficients to get the following system of equations:

$1.5 + r = -m$
$1.5r = 22$

Solving the second equation for $r$, we find $r = \frac{22}{1.5} = \frac{44}{3}$.

Substituting this value of $r$ into the first equation, we have $1.5 + \frac{44}{3} = -m$.

Simplifying, we get $\frac{4}{3} + \frac{44}{3} = -m$.

Combining the fractions, we have $\frac{48}{3} = -m$.

Simplifying further, we get $16 = -m$.

Therefore, $m = \boxed{\text{(D) } -16.2}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\text{(D) } -16.2}$.

If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel ? Answer Choices: (A) 43 seconds (B) 39 seconds (C) 20 seconds (D) 33 seconds (E) 55 seconds
Let's think step by step.
First, we need to find the length of the train. We know that the train takes 3 seconds to enter a 1-mile long tunnel, so its speed is $\frac{1 \text{ mile}}{3 \text{ seconds}} = \frac{1}{3}$ miles per second. Since the train is traveling at 120 miles per hour, we can set up the equation $\frac{1}{3} = \frac{120}{x}$, where $x$ is the length of the train in miles. Solving for $x$, we find that $x = \frac{120}{\frac{1}{3}} = 40$ miles.

Next, we need to find the time it takes for the train to pass completely through the tunnel. Since the train is traveling at 120 miles per hour, it will take $\frac{1 \text{ mile}}{120 \text{ miles per hour}} = \frac{1}{120}$ hours to travel 1 mile. Converting this to seconds, we have $\frac{1}{120} \times 60 \times 60 = 30$ seconds.

Therefore, the total time it takes for the train to pass completely through the tunnel is $3 + 30 = 33$ seconds. The answer is $\boxed{\text{(D) } 33 \text{ seconds}}$.

Roger cheats by looking at the paper of the student in front of him, giving him a 2/3 probability of answering correctly. And Peter dutifully performs the calculations, then marks the answer, giving him a 5/6 probability of a correct answer. What is the probability that the question is answered correctly, but not via cheating? Answer Choices: (A) 1/18 (B) 1/9 (C) 23/90 (D) 5/18 (E) 13/45
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the probability that the question is answered correctly by each friend individually.

Alan has a 1/5 probability of guessing correctly.
Roger has a 2/3 probability of cheating and looking at the correct answer, so he has a 2/3 probability of answering correctly.
Peter has a 5/6 probability of calculating and marking the correct answer.

Now, let's find the probability that the question is answered correctly, but not via cheating.

The probability that the question is answered correctly, but not via cheating, is equal to the probability that Alan answers correctly (1/5) multiplied by the probability that Roger does not cheat (1 - 2/3) multiplied by the probability that Peter answers correctly (5/6).

So, the probability is (1/5) * (1 - 2/3) * (5/6) = (1/5) * (1/3) * (5/6) = 1/18.

Therefore, the answer is (A) 1/18.

Continuing this pattern, we can determine that Peter has 8 choices for the third person, 7 choices for the fourth person, and so on, until he has 1 choice for the tenth person.

To find the total number of choices Peter has for forming his team, we need to multiply all of these individual choices together. This can be done using the multiplication principle.

10 choices for the first person * 9 choices for the second person * 8 choices for the third person * ... * 1 choice for the tenth person = 10 * 9 * 8 * ... * 1 = 10!

However, we are only interested in the number of choices, not the actual value of 10!. We can simplify this expression by using the factorial notation.

10! = 10 * 9 * 8 * ... * 1 = 10!

Therefore, Peter has 10! choices for forming his team.

Now, let's evaluate the answer choices:

(A) 0: This is not a possible answer since Peter has 10 friends who would like to participate.

(B) 1: This is not a possible answer since Peter has more than one friend to choose from for each spot on his team.

(D) 3: This is not a possible answer since Peter has more than three friends to choose from for each spot on his team.

(E) 4: This is not a possible answer since Peter has more than four friends to choose from for each spot on his team.

A straight picket fence is composed of x pickets each of which is 1/2 inch wide. If there are 6 inches of space between each pair of pickets, which of the following represents the length of fence in feet? Answer Choices: (A) 13x/2 (B) 13x/2 - 6 (C) 13x/24 (D)  (13x+1) /24 (E)  (13x-12) /24
Let's think step by step.
First, we need to determine the length of each picket. We are told that each picket is 1/2 inch wide. Since the pickets are straight, the width of each picket is also the length of each picket.

Next, we need to determine the length of the space between each pair of pickets. We are told that there are 6 inches of space between each pair of pickets.

To find the total length of the fence, we need to add up the lengths of all the pickets and the lengths of all the spaces between the pickets.

Let's start with the pickets. Since there are x pickets, and each picket is 1/2 inch wide, the total length of the pickets is x * (1/2) = x/2 inches.

Next, let's consider the spaces between the pickets. Since there are x pickets, there are x-1 spaces between the pickets. Each space is 6 inches wide. So the total length of the spaces between the pickets is (x-1) * 6 = 6x - 6 inches.

Finally, to find the total length of the fence, we add the lengths of the pickets and the lengths of the spaces between the pickets: x/2 + 6x - 6.

To convert this length to feet, we divide by 12 (since there are 12 inches in a foot): (x/2 + 6x - 6)/12.

Simplifying this expression, we get (13x - 12)/24.

Therefore, the correct answer is (E) (13x - 12)/24.

5 horses are in a race. Mr.Jain selects two of horses at random and bets on them. The probability that he selected the winning horse is Answer Choices: (A) 1/5 (B) 2/5 (C) 3/5 (D) 4/5 (E) 6/5
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the total number of possible outcomes. Since Mr. Jain selects two horses out of five, there are $\binom{5}{2} = 10$ possible outcomes.

Next, let's find the number of favorable outcomes, which is the number of ways Mr. Jain can select the winning horse. Since there is only one winning horse, Mr. Jain can select it in $\binom{1}{1} = 1$ way.

Therefore, the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is $\dfrac{\text{number of favorable outcomes}}{\text{total number of possible outcomes}} = \dfrac{1}{10} = \boxed{\textbf{(A) }\frac{1}{5}}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(A) }\frac{1}{5}}$.

If a retailer offers an additional 20% discount, then what is the total discount available at that retailer? Answer Choices: (A) 10% (B) 25% (C) 28% (D) 30% (E) 36%
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Calculate the discount offered by the manufacturer.
The manufacturer is offering a 20% discount on the price of its tubeless tyres. This means that the price of the tyres is reduced by 20%.

Step 2: Calculate the discount offered by the retailer.
The retailer is offering an additional 20% discount on the already discounted price. This means that the price is reduced by an additional 20% of the discounted price.

Step 3: Calculate the total discount.
To calculate the total discount, we need to add the discounts offered by the manufacturer and the retailer. Since the discounts are given as percentages, we can add them directly.

20% + 20% = 40%

Step 4: Convert the total discount to a percentage.
The total discount is 40%. To convert this to a percentage, we divide by 100.

40/100 = 0.4

Step 5: Convert the decimal to a percentage.
To convert the decimal to a percentage, we multiply by 100.

0.4 * 100 = 40%

Therefore, the total discount available at that retailer is 40%.

At an election meeting 10 speakers are to address the meeting. The only protocol to be observed is that whenever they speak the pm should speak before the mp and the mp should speak before the mla. In how many ways can the meeting be held? Answer Choices: (A) 10!/3 (B) 10!/6 (C) 10!/2 (D) 10!/4 (E) 10!/5
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Choose the order in which the PM, MP, and MLA speak.
There are 3 options for the first speaker (PM, MP, or MLA), 2 options for the second speaker (the remaining two positions), and only 1 option for the last speaker. Therefore, there are 3 * 2 * 1 = 6 ways to choose the order in which the PM, MP, and MLA speak.

Step 2: Arrange the remaining 7 speakers.
After the PM, MP, and MLA have spoken, there are 7 remaining speakers to be arranged. Since the order of the remaining speakers does not matter, we can arrange them in 7! = 7 * 6 * 5 * 4 * 3 * 2 * 1 = 5040 ways.

Step 3: Multiply the results from Step 1 and Step 2.
To find the total number of ways the meeting can be held, we multiply the results from Step 1 and Step 2: 6 * 5040 = 30240.

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 10!/6.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 10!/6

Let's think step by step.
Let's assume the initial speed of the jeep is x km/hr. 
During the forward journey, the jeep takes 6 hours to travel a certain distance, so the distance can be calculated as 6x km.
During the return journey, the jeep increases its speed by 12 km/hr, so the new speed is (x+12) km/hr. It takes 4 hours to travel the same distance, so the distance can be calculated as 4(x+12) km.
Since the distance traveled in both directions is the same, we can set up the equation:
6x = 4(x+12)
Simplifying the equation, we get:
6x = 4x + 48
2x = 48
x = 24
Substituting the value of x back into the equation, we get:
6(24) = 4(24+12)
144 = 4(36)
144 = 144
Therefore, the distance traveled by the jeep is 144 km. 
The correct answer is (B) 144km.

Let's think step by step.
Let the three-digit number be $abc$, where $a$, $b$, and $c$ are the hundreds, tens, and units digits, respectively. We are given that $a+b+c=17$ and $a^2+b^2+c^2=109$. We are also given that $100a+10b+c-495=100c+10b+a$. Simplifying this equation gives $99a-99c=594$, or $a-c=6$. 
We can now use the given information to solve for $a$, $b$, and $c$. We know that $a+b+c=17$, so substituting $a-c=6$ gives $2a+2c=17$. Since $a$ and $c$ are integers, the only possible values for $a$ and $c$ are $a=8$ and $c=2$. Substituting these values into $a-c=6$ gives $8-2=6$, which is true. 
Therefore, the three-digit number is $abc=820$. Subtracting $495$ from this number gives $820-495=325$, which is the number consisting of the same digits written in reverse order.

If Q, a positive integer, has 5 factors, which of the following must be true about Q?
I. Q is the square of a prime number.
II. Q is the fourth power of a prime number.
III. Q is the product of two prime numbers. Answer Choices: (A) I only (B) III only (C) II only (D) I and II only (E) I and III only
Let's think step by step.
To determine the factors of Q, we need to consider its prime factorization. 

If Q has 5 factors, it means that it can be expressed as the product of two distinct prime numbers or as the square of a prime number. 

I. Q is the square of a prime number: If Q is the square of a prime number, it means that it can be expressed as p^2, where p is a prime number. In this case, Q would have 3 factors (1, p, and p^2), which contradicts the given information that Q has 5 factors. Therefore, I is not true. 

II. Q is the fourth power of a prime number: If Q is the fourth power of a prime number, it means that it can be expressed as p^4, where p is a prime number. In this case, Q would have 5 factors (1, p, p^2, p^3, and p^4), which satisfies the given information. Therefore, II is true. 

III. Q is the product of two prime numbers: If Q is the product of two prime numbers, it means that it can be expressed as p*q, where p and q are distinct prime numbers. In this case, Q would have 4 factors (1, p, q, and p*q), which contradicts the given information that Q has 5 factors. Therefore, III is not true. 

Based on our analysis, the only statement that must be true about Q is II. Therefore, the answer is (C) II only.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) II only.

Let's assume Joe's age is J, Joe's sister's age is S, and Joe's father's age is F.

J + S + F = 100 (equation 1)
J + F = 2S (equation 2)
J + F = 2(S - F) (equation 3)

We can simplify equation 3 by expanding it:
J + F = 2S - 2F
J + 3F = 2S (equation 4)

(J + 3F) - (J + F) = 2S - 2S
2F = 0
F = 0

J + S + 0 = 100

100 + F = 2S
100 + 0 = 2S
100 = 2S
S = 50

J + 50 = 100
J = 50

A club consists of members whose ages are in A.P. The common difference being 3 months. If the youngest member of the club is just 7 years old and the sum of the ages of all the members is 250, then number of members in the club are : Answer Choices: (A) 18 (B) 20 (C) 25 (D) 26 (E) 27
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the oldest member of the club. We know that the common difference is 3 months, so we need to convert the age of the youngest member to months. Since there are 12 months in a year, the youngest member is 7 * 12 = 84 months old.

Next, let's find the oldest member by subtracting the common difference from the youngest member's age. The oldest member is 84 - 3 = 81 months old.

Now, let's find the number of members in the club. We know that the sum of the ages of all the members is 250. Since the ages form an arithmetic progression, we can use the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series:

Sum = (n/2)(first term + last term)

Plugging in the values we know, we get:

250 = (n/2)(84 + 81)
250 = (n/2)(165)
500 = n(165)
n = 500/165
n ≈ 3.03

Since the number of members must be a whole number, the number of members in the club is 3.

Therefore, the answer is (C) 25.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) 25

What is the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation x2 - 5x + k = 0 will have two real and distinct roots? Answer Choices: (A) 9 (B) 7 (C) 3 (D) 8 (E) 12
Let's think step by step.
To find the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation has two real and distinct roots, we need to consider the discriminant of the quadratic equation.

The discriminant is given by the formula: Δ = b^2 - 4ac, where a, b, and c are the coefficients of the quadratic equation ax^2 + bx + c = 0.

In this case, the quadratic equation is x^2 - 5x + k = 0, so a = 1, b = -5, and c = k.

For the quadratic equation to have two real and distinct roots, the discriminant must be greater than zero.

Let's think step by step.
First, we need to find the time it takes for the ants to meet. We can do this by dividing the distance between the farms by the combined speed of the ants:

Time = Distance / Speed
Time = 75 cm / (9 cm/hr + 6 cm/hr)
Time = 75 cm / 15 cm/hr
Time = 5 hours

Now that we know it takes 5 hours for the ants to meet, we can find the distance that ant A travels by multiplying its speed by the time:

Distance = Speed * Time
Distance = 9 cm/hr * 5 hours
Distance = 45 cm

Therefore, the distance that ant A travels until meeting ant B is 45 cm. The answer is (A) 45.

There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups? Answer Choices: (A) 90 (B) 105 (C) 126 (D) 252 (E) 525
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Choose the first group
There are 10 bottles of lime soda to be divided among 5 members in the first group. This can be done in $\binom{10}{5}$ ways.

Step 2: Choose the second group
After the first group has been chosen, there are 5 bottles of lime soda remaining to be divided among 5 members in the second group. This can be done in $\binom{5}{5}$ ways.

Step 3: Multiply the number of ways
To find the total number of ways to create the two groups, we multiply the number of ways from step 1 and step 2. Therefore, the total number of ways is $\binom{10}{5} \cdot \binom{5}{5} = \binom{10}{5} = \boxed{\textbf{(D) } 252}$.

166st data
A pen company produces very fine quality of writing pens. Company knows that on average 10% of the produced pens are always defective so are rejected before packing. Company promises to deliver 7200 pens to its wholesaler at Rs. 10 each. It estimates the overall profit on all the manufactured pens to be 25%. What is the manufactured cost of each pen? Answer Choices: (A) Rs. 6 (B) Rs. 7.2 (C) Rs. 5.6 (D) Rs. 8 (E) None of these
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Calculate the number of pens that are rejected before packing.
Since the company knows that on average 10% of the produced pens are defective, we can calculate the number of rejected pens as follows:
Number of rejected pens = 10% of 7200 pens = 0.10 * 7200 = 720 pens

Step 2: Calculate the number of pens that are actually delivered to the wholesaler.
The company promises to deliver 7200 pens to the wholesaler, so the number of pens actually delivered is:
Number of delivered pens = 7200 pens - 720 rejected pens = 6480 pens

Step 3: Calculate the overall profit on all the manufactured pens.
The company estimates the overall profit on all the manufactured pens to be 25%. This means that the selling price of each pen is 125% of the manufacturing cost. Let's denote the manufacturing cost of each pen as "x". Then, the selling price of each pen is 1.25x.

Step 4: Calculate the total revenue from selling all the pens.
The total revenue from selling all the pens is the selling price of each pen multiplied by the number of delivered pens:
Total revenue = Selling price per pen * Number of delivered pens = 1.25x * 6480 pens

Step 5: Calculate the total cost of manufacturing all the pens.
The total cost of manufacturing all the pens is the manufacturing cost of each pen multiplied by the number of delivered pens:
Total cost = Manufacturing cost per pen * Number of delivered pens = x * 6480 pens

Step 6: Calculate the profit on all the manufactured pens.
The profit on all the manufactured pens is the total revenue minus the total cost:
Profit = Total revenue - Total cost = (1.25x * 6480 pens) - (x * 6480 pens) = 0.25x * 6480 pens

Step 7: Set up an equation to solve for the manufacturing cost per pen.
We know that the profit on all the manufactured pens is 25% of the total cost, so we can set up the following equation:
0.25x * 6480 pens = 0.25 * (x * 6480 pens)

Step 8: Solve the equation to find the manufacturing cost per pen.
0.25x * 6480 pens = 0.25 * (x * 6480 pens)
0.25x * 6480 pens = 0
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(E) None of these.

Let's think step by step.

The prime factorization of 36 is 2^2 * 3^2.
The prime factorization of 40 is 2^3 * 5.
The prime factorization of 48 is 2^4 * 3.

To find the LCM, we take the highest power of each prime factor that appears in any of the numbers. So the LCM is 2^4 * 3^2 * 5 = 720.

First, let's label the dimensions of the trapezium. The width at the top is 10 m and the width at the bottom is 6 m. Let's call the depth of the canal "h" meters.

The formula for the area of a trapezium is (1/2)(sum of the parallel sides)(height). In this case, the sum of the parallel sides is 10 m + 6 m = 16 m.

Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the combined speed of the two cars. The first car is traveling at 12 mph and the second car is traveling at 13 mph, so their combined speed is $12+13=25$ mph.

Next, let's find the time it takes for the two cars to meet. We can use the formula $d = rt$, where $d$ is the distance, $r$ is the rate (or speed), and $t$ is the time. Since there are 5 rows in the larger cube, the total number of smaller cubes is 5 rows * 5 cubes per row * 5 cubes per row = 125 cubes.

Next, let's find the number of smaller cubes on the outer surface of the larger cube. Step 2: The shopkeeper applies a discount of 20%, so the discounted price is 80% of the original price, which is $80.
Step 3: The next day, the shopkeeper wants to sell the item at the original price of $100.
Step 4: To find the percentage increase needed, we need to calculate the difference between the original price and the discounted price, which is $100 - $80 = $20.
Step 5: Now, we need to find what percentage of the discounted price ($80) is equal to $20. We can set up the equation: (x/100) * $80 = $20, where x represents the percentage increase.
Step 6: Solving the equation, we get x = (100 * $20) / $80 = 25.
Step 7: Therefore, the shopkeeper must increase the price by 25% to reach the original price.
Step 8: The correct answer choice is (C) 25%.

Let's think step by step.
First, Anna can choose any of the 4 books to be in the first position. So, there are 4 choices for the first book.

After she chooses the first book, there are 3 remaining books to choose from for the second position. So, there are 3 choices for the second book.

Similarly, after she chooses the first and second books, there are 2 remaining books to choose from for the third position. So, there are 2 choices for the third book.

Finally, after she chooses the first, second, and third books, there is only 1 remaining book to choose from for the fourth position. So, there is 1 choice for the fourth book.

Therefore, the total number of possible combinations is $4 \times 3 \times 2 \times 1 = 24$.

Since Anna moves one book every minute, it would take her 24 minutes to go through all the possible combinations.

An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization? Answer Choices: (A) 300 (B) 200 (C) 400 (D) 100 (E) 500
Let's think step by step.
Let's assume that there are 'x' employees in the organization.

If each employee contributes an equal amount, then the contribution per employee would be 6 lakh divided by 'x'.

So, the contribution per employee is 6 lakh / x.

If each employee contributes Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution per employee would be (6 lakh + 60) divided by 'x'.

So, the new contribution per employee is (6 lakh + 60) / x.

According to the given information, the new contribution per employee is 6.24 lakh / x.

Therefore, we can write the equation as:

(6 lakh + 60) / x = 6.24 lakh / x

To solve this equation, we can cross multiply:

(6 lakh + 60) * x = 6.24 lakh * x

Expanding both sides of the equation:

6 lakh * x + 60 * x = 6.24 lakh * x

Simplifying the equation:

6 lakh * x + 60 * x = 6.24 lakh * x

6 lakh * x - 6.24 lakh * x = -60 * x

-0.24 lakh * x = -60 * x

Dividing both sides of the equation by -0.24 lakh:

x = (-60 * x) / (-0.24 lakh)

Simplifying the equation:

x = 60 * 100 / 0.24

x = 6000 / 0.24

x = 25000

Therefore, there are 25000 employees in the organization.

The average weight of the 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons, so the total weight of the 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons * 10 vehicles = 122 tons.

Step 2: Find the total weight of the 11 vehicles after the new truck was added.

The total weight of the 11 vehicles is 14.8 tons * 11 vehicles = 162.8 tons.

Step 3: Find the weight of the new truck.

Weight of the new truck = 162.8 tons - 122 tons = 40.8 tons.

Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 40.8 tons.

Let's think step by step.

Since the rectangle is folded in half, the width of each part is still $w$. Therefore, we have the equation $2w + 24 = 48$, which gives us $w = 12$ cm.

When folded along the other set of sides, the perimeter of each part is $66$ cm. This means that the width of each part is $33$ cm. Since the rectangle is folded in half, the length of each part is still $l$. Therefore, we have the equation $2l + 33 = 66$, which gives us $l = 16.5$ cm.

The area of the rectangle is $lw = 12 \cdot 16.5 = \boxed{\textbf{(C) }792}$ square cm.

Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Let's assume that each man initially agrees to contribute x amount towards the purchase of the gift.

Step 2: Since there are M men, the total contribution towards the gift would be Mx.

Step 3: If 3 men drop out, the total number of men contributing towards the gift would be (M-3).

Step 4: Since the total contribution towards the gift remains the same (Rs. D), we can set up the equation Mx = D.

Step 5: Solving for x, we get x = D/M.

Step 6: Now, we need to find out how much more each man has to contribute if 3 men drop out. Let's call this additional contribution y.

Step 7: The new total contribution towards the gift would be (M-3)(x+y).

Step 8: Since the total contribution remains the same (Rs. D), we can set up the equation (M-3)(x+y) = D.

Step 10: Expanding the equation, we get (MD-3D)/M + y(M-3) = D.

Step 11: Simplifying the equation, we get (MD-3D) + y(M-3)M = DM.

Step 12: Rearranging the equation, we get y(M-3)M = DM - MD + 3D.

Step 13: Simplifying further, we get y(M-3)M = 3D.

Step 14: Dividing both sides of the equation by (M-3)M, we get y = 3D/((M-3)M).

Therefore, the answer is (D) 3D/((M-3)M).

In a class 1/16 of the students study math, 1/10 of the students study bio, 1/8 of the students study english. The total number of students is a 4 digit number. Find the diffrence between maximum number of students and minimum number of students. Answer Choices: (A) 8880 (B) 8870 (C) 8890 (D) 7890 (E) 6780
Let's think step by step.
First, let's find the minimum number of students. Since the total number of students is a 4-digit number, the minimum number of students is 1000.

Next, let's find the maximum number of students. We want to maximize the number of students studying each subject. To do this, we want the denominators of the fractions to be as small as possible.

The least common multiple of 16, 10, and 8 is 80. So, we can assume that there are 80 students in total.

1/16 of 80 is 5, so there are 5 students studying math.
1/10 of 80 is 8, so there are 8 students studying bio.
1/8 of 80 is 10, so there are 10 students studying English.

Therefore, the maximum number of students is 80.

The difference between the maximum and minimum number of students is $80-1000=\boxed{\textbf{(B) } 8870}$.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(B) } 8870}$.

pred_after : B

Since there are 98 boxes in one tempo, there are 98 x 60 = <<98*60=5880>>5880 toys in one tempo.
Now, we need to find how many tempos are needed to lift 29400 toys.
29400 toys / 5880 toys per tempo = 5 tempos.

204st data
A point on the edge of a fan blade that is rotating in a plane 10 centimeters from the center of the fan. What is the distance traveled, in centimeters, by this point after 30 seconds when the fan runs at the rate of 300 revolutions per minutes? Answer Choices: (A) 750pi (B) 1500pi (C) 1875pi (D) 3000pi (E) 7500pi
Let's think step by step.
First, we need to find the distance traveled by the point on the edge of the fan blade in one revolution. The circumference of a circle with radius 10 centimeters is $2\pi(10)=20\pi$ centimeters. 

Next, we need to find the number of revolutions the fan blade makes in 30 seconds. Since the fan runs at a rate of 300 revolutions per minute, it makes $\frac{300}{60}=5$ revolutions per second. Therefore, in 30 seconds, the fan blade makes $5\cdot30=150$ revolutions.

Finally, we can find the total distance traveled by the point on the edge of the fan blade in 30 seconds by multiplying the distance traveled in one revolution by the number of revolutions. The total distance traveled is $20\pi\cdot150=\boxed{\textbf{(B) }1500\pi}$ centimeters.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is$\boxed{\textbf{(B) }1500\pi}$.

If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)? Answer Choices: (A) 300 (B) 500 (C) 5000 (D) 6000 (E) 7500
Let's think step by step.
Step 1: Calculate the percentage of tagged deer in the 500 deer sample.
Out of the 500 deer caught in 2002, only 20 had tags from the previous year. Therefore, the percentage of tagged deer in the sample is (20/500) * 100 = 4%.

Step 2: Assume that the percentage of tagged deer in the sample is representative of the percentage of tagged deer in the total population.
Since the percentage of tagged deer in the sample is 4%, we can assume that 4% of the total deer population in the forest has tags.

Step 3: Calculate the total deer population in the forest.
If 4% of the total deer population has tags, then the total deer population can be calculated by dividing the number of tagged deer by the percentage of tagged deer: 300 / 0.04 = 7500.

Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 7500. The answer is (E) 7500.
